## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and time. The relationship likely involves nonlinear restoring forces, possible damping, and/or external driving terms common in oscillator equations of motion.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (Duffing with periodic driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Full cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring + damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with driving)
- Quintic Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve oscillator symmetry; even powers (x²) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Products of position powers with velocity (e.g., x²*v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators
- Sinusoidal dependence on time (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Sinusoidal dependence on position (sin(c*x)) suggests a periodic potential like a pendulum rather than polynomial restoring force
- Time appearing only inside trigonometric functions suggests autonomous dynamics with external forcing rather than explicit time dependence of parameters
- Negative coefficient on the linear x term combined with positive coefficient on x³ indicates a double-well (bistable) potential
- Terms like (1 - x²)*v are hallmarks of limit cycle oscillators where damping switches sign depending on amplitude
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests a conservative or dissipative autonomous system where energy analysis applies
- Product terms x*v suggest forces derivable from velocity-dependent potentials or coordinate-momentum coupling
